--- page 64 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
DRAFT ORDINANCE
Amending Chapter 7.41 “Tobacco Retailer Permit” of the San Mateo Municipal Code 
WHEREAS, the City of San Mateo has authorized personnel from the County of San Mateo to administer 
and enforce Municipal Code Chapter 7.41 “Tobacco Retailer Permit” on behalf of the City; and
WHEREAS, the San Mateo County Board of Supervisors recently adopted an ordinance to amend the San 
Mateo County Code related to Tobacco Retailer Permits; and 
WHEREAS, San Mateo County has indicated it will continue to administer a tobacco retailer permit 
program for those cities which adopt the County’s same comprehensive ordinance in its entirety; and 
WHEREAS, the San Mateo Police Department wishes to continue to partner with the County to 
administer a tobacco retailer permit program in the City of San Mateo; and
WHEREAS, the proposed amendments to Chapter 7.41 will add definitions to incorporate best practices 
across the state, strengthen ordinance language to reduce youth access to tobacco products, and make the San 
Mateo Municipal Code consistent with the San Mateo County Code, thereby promoting more efficient 
administration and enforcement.
NOW, THEREFORE, THE COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO ORDAINS AS FOLLOWS:
Section 1. Section 7.41.005 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is added to Chapter 7.41 as follows:
7.41.005 Definitions.
(a) "Characterizing Flavor" means a distinguishable taste or aroma, or both, other than the taste or 
aroma of tobacco, imparted by a Tobacco Product or any byproduct produced by the Tobacco Product. 
Characterizing flavors include, but are not limited to, tastes or aroma relating to any fruit, chocolate, vanilla, 
honey, candy, cocoa, dessert, alcoholic beverage, menthol, mint, wintergreen, herb, or spice. A Tobacco Product 
shall not be determined to have a Characterizing Flavor solely because of the use of additives or flavorings or the 
provision of ingredient information. Rather, it is the presence of a distinguishable taste or aroma, or both, as 
described in the first sentence of this definition, that constitutes a Characterizing Flavor.
(b) "Constituent" means any ingredient, substance, chemical, or compound, other than tobacco, water, 
or reconstituted tobacco sheet that is added by the manufacturer to a Tobacco Product during the processing, 
manufacture, or packing of the Tobacco Product.
(c) “Consumer” means a person who purchases a Tobacco Product for consumption.
(d) “Coupon” means any voucher, rebate, card, paper, note, form, statement, ticket, image, or other 
issue, whether in paper, digital, or other form, used for commercial purposes to obtain an article, product, 
service, or accommodation without charge or at a discounted price.
64 of 265

--- page 65 ---
(e) “Director” means the Chief of San Mateo County Health, or designee.
(f) "Distinguishable" means perceivable by either the sense of smell or taste.
(g) “Electronic Smoking Device” means any device that may be used to deliver any aerosolized or 
vaporized substance to the person inhaling from the device, including, but not limited to, an e-cigarette, e-cigar, 
e-pipe, vape pen, or e- hookah. Electronic smoking device includes any component, part, or accessory of the 
device, and also includes any substance that may be aerosolized or vaporized by such device, whether or not the 
substance contains nicotine, and whether natural or synthetic. “Electronic Smoking Device” does not include any 
product that has been approved by the United States Food and Drug Administration for sale as a tobacco 
cessation product or for other therapeutic purposes where such product is marketed and sold solely for such an 
approved purpose.
(h) "Flavored Tobacco Product" means any Tobacco Product that contains a Constituent that imparts a 
Characterizing Flavor.
(i) “Full Retail Price” means the price listed for a Tobacco Product on its Packaging or on any related 
shelving, advertising, or display where the Tobacco Product is sold or offered for Sale, plus all applicable taxes 
and fees if such taxes and fees are not included in the listed price.
(j) “Labeling” means written, printed, pictorial, or graphic matter upon any Tobacco Product or any of its 
packaging.
(k) “Packaging” means a pack, box, carton, or container of any kind or, if no other container, any 
wrapping (including cellophane) in which a Tobacco Product is sold, or offered for Sale, to a Consumer.
(l) “Permit” or “Tobacco Retailer Permit” means a valid permit issued by the Director to a Person to act 
as a Tobacco Retailer.
(m) “Person” means any natural person, partnership, cooperative association, corporation, personal 
representative, receiver, trustee, assignee, or any other entity.
(n) "Pharmacy" means any retail establishment in which the profession of pharmacy is practiced by a 
pharmacist licensed by the State of California in accordance with the Business and Professions Code and where 
prescription pharmaceuticals are offered for Sale, regardless of whether the retail establishment Sells other 
retail goods in addition to prescription pharmaceuticals.
(o) “Sale” or “Sell” means transfer to, exchange, barter, or distribute for a commercial purpose.
(p) “Self-Service Display” shall be defined as the open display or storage of Tobacco Products in a 
manner that is physically accessible to the general public without the assistance of the retailer or employee of 
the retailer and a direct face-to-face transfer between the purchaser and the retailer or employee of the 
retailer. A vending machine is a form of self-service display.
(q) “Tobacco Paraphernalia” means any item designed or marketed for the consumption, use, or 
preparation of Tobacco Products.
65 of 265

--- page 66 ---
(r) “Tobacco" or "Tobacco Product(s)" means:
(1) any product containing, made of, or derived from tobacco or nicotine, whether natural or 
synthetic, that is intended for human consumption or is likely to be consumed, whether inhaled, 
absorbed, or ingested by any other means, including but not limited to, a cigarette, a cigar, pipe 
tobacco, chewing tobacco, snuff, or snus;
(2) any electronic smoking device and any substances that may be aerosolized or vaporized by 
such device, whether or not the substance contains nicotine, and whether natural or synthetic; or
(3) any component, part, or accessory of (1) or (2), whether or not any of these contains tobacco 
or nicotine, whether natural or synthetic, including but not limited to filters, rolling papers, blunt or 
hemp wraps, hookahs, mouthpieces, and pipes.
(4) “Tobacco Product” does not include any product that has been approved by the United 
States Food and Drug Administration for sale as a tobacco cessation product or for other therapeutic 
purposes where such product is marketed and sold solely for such an approved purpose. 
(s) “Tobacco Product Flavor Enhancer” means a product designed, manufactured, produced, marketed 
or Sold to produce a Characterizing Flavor when added to a Tobacco Product.
(t) “Tobacco Retailer” means any Person who Sells, or offers for Sale, Tobacco Products. This definition is 
without regard to the quantity of Tobacco Products sold or offered for Sale.
(u) “Youth-Populated Area” means a parcel of real property that is occupied, in whole or in part, by any 
of the following:
(1) a private or public school that educates children in grades kindergarten through high school;
(2) a library that is open to the public;
(3) a playground that is open to the public;
(4) a youth center, defined as a facility where children ages 6 to 17 come together for programs 
and activities;
(5) a recreation facility open to the public, defined as an area, place, structure, or other facility 
that is used either permanently or temporarily for community recreation, even though it may be used 
for other purposes. “Recreation facility” includes, but is not limited to, a gymnasium, playing court, 
playing field, and swimming pool;
(6) a public or private college or university that serves as an institution for education beyond the 
high school level;
(7) a licensed child-care facility or preschool, other than a small-family day care home or a large-
family daycare home as defined in California Health & Safety Code § 1596.78.
66 of 265

--- page 67 ---
Section 2. Section 7.41.010 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:
7.41.010 Requirement for a Permit.
(a) No Tobacco Retailer or other Person shall Sell or offer for Sale any Tobacco Product without a current 
and valid Tobacco Retailer Permit from San Mateo County for each location where such activities are conducted.
(b) Permits are valid for one year and must be timely renewed annually by the Permit holder in order to 
continue to sell or offer for sale any Tobacco Product. A Retailer must obtain a separate Permit for each location 
at which any Tobacco Product will be sold, offered for sale or distributed. A Permit that is not renewed in a 
timely manner shall expire at the end of its term, and the Tobacco Retailer must obtain a new Permit prior to 
any further sale, offer for sale, or distribution of any Tobacco Product.
(c) No Tobacco Retailer shall violate, or cause or allow the Tobacco Retailer’s agents or employees to 
violate, any provision of this Chapter or any other local, state, or federal law applicable to Tobacco Products or 
Tobacco Retailing.
(d) Tobacco Retailers are responsible for the actions of their employees and agents relating to the sale, 
offer to sell, and furnishing of tobacco products at the retail location. The sale of any tobacco product by an 
employee shall be considered an act of the tobacco retailer and the permit holder shall be responsible for any 
monetary penalties levied.
(e) Nothing in this Chapter shall be construed to penalize the purchase, use, or possession of a Tobacco 
Product by any Person not engaged in Tobacco Retailing.
Section 3. Section 7.41.015 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is added to Chapter 7.41 as follows:
7.41.015 Permit Conveys a Limited, Conditional Privilege.
Nothing in this Chapter shall be construed to grant any Person or entity obtaining and maintaining a 
Permit any status or right other than the limited, conditional privilege to Sell Tobacco Products and act as a 
Tobacco Retailer at the location in the County identified on the face of the Permit for the period of time shown 
on the Permit. All Permits are issued subject to the County’s right to amend this Chapter from time to time, and 
Retailers shall comply with all provisions of this Chapter, as amended.
Section 4. Section 7.41.020 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:
7.41.020 Application, Issuance and Renewal Procedure.
(a) Application for a Tobacco Retailer's Permit or the renewal of a Tobacco Retailer Permit shall be 
submitted in the name of the Person proposing to conduct retail sales of Tobacco Products, referred to herein as 
the “Applicant,” and shall be signed by such Person or an authorized agent thereof. All applications shall be 
submitted to the Director on a form supplied by the Director and contain, at a minimum, the following 
information:
(1) The name, address, and telephone number of the Applicant;
67 of 265

--- page 68 ---
(2) The business name, address, and telephone number of the location where Tobacco Products 
are proposed to be sold, offered for sale or distributed by the Applicant; and
(3) Proof that the location for which a Tobacco Retailer’s Permit is sought has been issued a 
valid state license for the sale of Tobacco Products, if the Tobacco Retailer sells products that require 
such license;
(4) A statement whether or not the Tobacco Retailer or any agent of the Retailer has been found 
to have violated this Chapter or other applicable law governing Tobacco Products or Tobacco Retailing 
and, if so, the dates and locations of all such violations within the previous five years; and
(5) Such other information as the Director determines is necessary for implementation of this 
Chapter.
(6) An application for a new or renewal Permit will be denied if there are any outstanding fines 
or late fees issued by the Director, or during any period of suspension.
(7) It is the responsibility of each Permit holder to be informed regarding all laws applicable to 
Tobacco Retailing, including those laws affecting the issuance of a Tobacco Retailer Permit. No Permit 
holder may rely on the issuance of a Permit as a determination by San Mateo County that the Permit 
holder has complied with all laws applicable to Tobacco Retailing. A Permit issued contrary to this 
Chapter or any other law, or on the basis of false or misleading information supplied by the Applicant, 
shall be revoked. Nothing in this Chapter shall be construed to vest in any person or entity obtaining or 
maintaining a Tobacco Retailer’s Permit any status or right to act as a Tobacco Retailer in contravention 
of any provision of law.
Section 5. Section 7.41.030 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:
7.41.030 Display of Permit.
Upon receipt of an application for a Ttobacco Rretailer's Ppermit in compliance with the requirements of 
this Chapter, the Director or designee may issue a Ppermit which, if issued, must be prominently displayed in a 
publicly visible location at the location where Ttobacco Pproduct Ssales are conducted and permitted.
Section 6. Section 7.41.031 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is added to Chapter 7.41 as follows:
7.41.031 Prohibitions Regarding Coupons, Discounts, Pharmacies, Flavored Tobacco, and Electronic Smoking 
Devices.
(a) No Tobacco Retailer shall do any of the following:
(1) Honor or redeem, or offer to honor or redeem, a Coupon to allow a Consumer to purchase a 
Tobacco Product for less than Full Retail Price;
68 of 265

--- page 69 ---
(2) Sell any Tobacco Product to a Consumer through a multiple package discount or otherwise 
provide any such product to a Consumer for less than the Full Retail Price in consideration for the 
purchase of any Tobacco Product or any other item; or
(3) Provide any free or discounted item to a Consumer in consideration for the purchase of any 
Tobacco Product.
(b) No Person, Tobacco Retailer or other legal entity shall sell or distribute to a person any electronic 
smoking device that delivers natural or synthetic nicotine or any other substance(s) to the person inhaling from 
the device.  This includes any component, part, or accessory intended or reasonably expected to be used with 
the electronic device, whether or not sold separately.
(c) No Person or Tobacco Retailer shall sell or offer to sell any Flavored Tobacco Product or Tobacco 
Product Flavor Enhancer. There shall be a rebuttable presumption that a Tobacco Product is a Flavored Tobacco 
Product if a manufacturer or any of the manufacturer's agents or employees, in the course of their agency or 
employment, has made a statement or claim directed to consumers or to the public that the Tobacco Product 
has or produces a Characterizing Flavor including, but not limited to, text, color, and/or images on the product's 
labeling or packaging that are used to explicitly or implicitly communicate that the Tobacco Product has a 
Characterizing Flavor.
(d) No Pharmacy or Pharmacy employee or agent shall sell or offer to sell any Tobacco Product. The 
Director shall not issue any new, or renew any existing, Tobacco Retailer Permit for any Pharmacy.
(e) Subdivisions (b) and (c) of this Section shall not apply to the duty- free stores located at the San 
Francisco International Airport.
Section 7. Section 7.41.032 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is added to Chapter 7.41 as follows:
7.41.032 Packaging and Labeling.
No Tobacco Retailer or other Person shall Sell or offer for Sale any Tobacco Product to any Consumer 
unless the Tobacco Product (1) is Sold in the original manufacturer’s Packaging intended for Sale to 
Consumers; (2) conforms to all applicable federal Labeling requirements; and (3) conforms to all 
applicable child-resistant packaging requirements.
Section 8. Section 7.41.033 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is added to Chapter 7.41 as follows:
7.41.033 Self-Service Displays Prohibited; On-site, In-Person Sales Required.
(a) Tobacco Retailing by means of a Self-Service Display is prohibited.
(b) All Sales of Tobacco Products and Tobacco Paraphernalia shall be conducted in- person, over the 
counter, in the permitted location.
Section 9. Section 7.41.034 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is added to Chapter 7.41 as follows:
69 of 265

--- page 70 ---
7.41.034 Notice of Minimum Age for Purchase of Tobacco Products
Tobacco Retailers shall post conspicuously, at each point of purchase, a notice stating that Selling 
Tobacco Products to anyone under 21 years of age is illegal and subject to penalties. The form and content of 
such notice shall be subject to the approval of the Director.
Section 10. Section 7.41.035 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is added to Chapter 7.41 as follows:
7.41.035 Positive Identification Required.
No Tobacco Retailer or other Person shall Sell or offer to Sell a Tobacco Product to another Person 
without first verifying by means of government-issued photographic identification that the recipient is at least 
the minimum legal sales age required under state law to purchase a Tobacco Product.
Section 11. Section 7.41.036 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is added to Chapter 7.41 as follows:
7.41.036 Minimum Age for Individuals Selling Tobacco Products.
No Tobacco Retailer shall allow, at its Retail location, any individual who is younger than 21 years of age 
to Sell or offer to Sell Tobacco Products.
Section 12. Section 7.41.037 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is added to Chapter 7.41 as follows:
7.41.037 Display or Offers to Sell Tobacco Products Without Tobacco Retailer Permit Prohibited
(a) A Tobacco Retailer without a current valid Permit:
(1) Shall keep all Tobacco Products out of public view. The public display of Tobacco Products in 
violation of this provision shall constitute Tobacco Retailing without a Permit.
(2) Shall not display any advertisement relating to Tobacco Products that offers the Sale of such 
products from the Tobacco Retailer’s location.
Section 13. Section 7.41.038 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is added to Chapter 7.41 as follows:
7.41.038 Limits on Eligibility for a Permit.
(a) No Tobacco Retailer’s Permit may be issued to authorize Tobacco Retailing at or from other than a 
fixed location. For example, Sales by Persons on foot or from vehicles or other forms of mobile vending are 
prohibited.
(b) No Tobacco Retailer’s Permit may be issued to authorize Sales of Tobacco Products at a temporary 
event, such as flea markets and farmers’ markets.
(c) No new Tobacco Retailer Permit may be issued to authorize Tobacco Product Sales at any location 
within 1,000 feet of a Youth-Populated Area, as measured by a straight line from the nearest point of the 
70 of 265

--- page 71 ---
property line of any parcel on which a Youth-Populated Area is located and any point along the property line of 
the parcel on which the Permit applicant has or proposes to locate the business.
(d) No new Tobacco Retailer’s Permit may be issued for a location which is within 500 feet of a location 
already occupied by another Tobacco Retailer, as measured by a straight line from the nearest point of the 
property line of the parcel on which the applicant’s business is located to the nearest point of the property line 
of the parcel on which an existing Tobacco Retailer’s business is located.
(e) Tobacco Retailers with a current and valid Permit as of the date of adoption of this ordinance shall be 
exempt from subsections (c) and (d) of this Section unless the existing Tobacco Retailer fails to timely renew the 
Permit prior to its annual expiration.
(f) The Sale of Tobacco Products and accessories is prohibited in County owned structures and in any 
area of a structure leased by the County, wherever located.
Section 14. Section 7.41.040 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:
7.41.040 Fees for Permit
Tobacco retailers shall pay all applicable fees at the rates set forth in Section 5.64.070 of the San Mateo 
County Code.  Fees shall be used by the Director to administer and enforce this chapter.
Section 15. Section 7.41.050 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:
7.41.050 Permit is Nontransferable.
(a) Tobacco Retailer Permits are nontransferable as between Persons, locations, or otherwise. Any 
attempted transfer shall render the Permit null and void.
(b) Notwithstanding any other provision of this Chapter, prior violations of this Chapter at a location 
shall continue to be counted against that location and Permit ineligibility and suspension periods shall continue 
to apply to that location unless:
(1) One hundred percent of the interest in the stock, assets, or income of the business, other 
than a security interest for the repayment of debt, has been transferred to the new owner(s); and
(2) The County is provided with clear and convincing evidence, including an affidavit, that the 
business has been acquired in an Arm's Length Transaction. An Arm’s Length Transaction, for the 
purposes of this section, means a transaction in which two or more unrelated and unaffiliated parties 
agree on the transfer in question; the parties act independently and in their own self-interest; and the 
parties have equal bargaining power and symmetric information, leading the parties to agree upon fair-
market terms.
Section 16. Section 7.41.060 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:

7.41.060 Enforcement.
(a) The Director or the Director’s designee shall enforce this Chapter consistent with the provisions

7.41.065 Public Nuisance.

administrative, and criminal remedies and penalties according to the provisions and procedures of contained in 
the San Mateo County Code and state law, including but not limited to, an action for abatement or injunctive 
relief.
Section 18. Section 7.41.068 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is added to Chapter 7.41 as follows:
7.41.068 Compliance Monitoring.
(a) Compliance with this Chapter shall be monitored by the Director. In addition, any peace officer may 
enforce the provisions of this Chapter. The Director may designate additional persons to monitor and facilitate 
compliance with this Chapter.
(b) Individuals designated to enforce the provisions of this Chapter shall inspect each Tobacco Retailer 
annuallyat least two times during each twelve-month period to determine if the Tobacco Retailer is complying 
with all applicable laws. Compliance checks shall take place during normal business hours, with or without 
notice. If a violation has occurred, the Tobacco Retailer shall be inspected again within three months. All 
permitted premises must be open to inspection by designated persons during regular business hours.
(c) Nothing in this section shall create a right of action in any Tobacco Retailer or other person or entity 
against the County or its agents.
Section 19. Section 7.41.070 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:
7.41.070 Suspension or Revocation of Permit.
(a) Grounds for Suspension or Revocation.
(1) A Tobacco Retailer Permit may be suspended or revoked, as set forth below in 
subdivision (b), if any court of a competent jurisdiction determines, or the Director finds, based on 
a preponderance of the evidence after notice and opportunity for the Tobacco Retailer to be heard, 
that either of the following violations have occurred:
72 of 265

--- page 73 ---
(A) After the Permit was issued it is determined that the Application for the Permit is 
incomplete or inaccurate.
(B) The Tobacco Retailer or Tobacco Retailer’s agent has violated any of the 
requirements, conditions, or prohibitions of this Chapter or any applicable local, state, or federal 
tobacco-related law.
(2) Notwithstanding the foregoing, a Tobacco Retailer Permit shall be suspended or revoked, 
for the maximum time periods and as set forth in subdivision (b), if any court of competent 
jurisdiction determines, or the Director finds, based on a preponderance of evidence and after 
notice and opportunity for the Tobacco Retailer to be heard, that the Tobacco Retailer, or any agent 
or employee of the Tobacco Retailer, has Sold Tobacco Products to any Person(s) under the age of 
21 years.
(b) Time Period of Suspension of Permit.
(1) Upon the first violation within any sixty (60) month period, the Permit to Sell Tobacco 
Products may be suspended for up to 30 days.
(2) Upon the second violation within any sixty (60) month period, the Permit to Sell Tobacco 
Products may be suspended for up to 90 days.
(3) Upon the third violation within any sixty (60) month period, the Permit to Sell Tobacco 
Products may be suspended for up to one year.
(4) Upon the fourth violation within any sixty (60) month period, the Permit to Sell Tobacco 
Products shall be revoked. If a Permit is revoked, the Retailer shall not be eligible for a new 
Permit for a period of five (5) years after the effective date of revocation.
(c) Effective Date of Suspension or Revocation. Within ten (10) calendar days of the hearing, the 
Director shall issue written findings and an order regarding the suspension or revocation, which order will be 
effective ten (10) calendar days from the date such order was sent by certified mail to the Retailer, unless a 
timely appeal is filed in accordance with subsection (d).
(d) Appeal of Suspension or Revocation.  The decision of the Director is appealable to the San Mateo 
County Licensing Board and the procedural rules of the San Mateo County Licensing Board shall govern 
hearings on all appeals of suspensions and revocations.
(1) An appeal must be in writing, be addressed to the Director and be hand- delivered to the 
offices of the Division of Environmental Health.
(2) An appeal must be received by the Director before the effective date of suspension or 
revocation provided by subsection (c) in order to be considered.
(3) The filing of a timely appeal will stay a suspension or revocation pending a decision on the 
appeal by the San Mateo County Licensing Board.
73 of 265

--- page 74 ---
(4) The decision of the San Mateo County Licensing Board shall be a final administrative 
order, with no further administrative right of appeal.
Section 20. Section 7.41.080 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:
7.41.080 Administrative Fine.
(a) Grounds for Fine. A fine mayshall be imposed on a Tobacco Retailer upon findings made by 
the Director, based on a preponderance of the evidence, that any Tobacco Retailer, or any agent or 
employee of the Tobacco Retailer, has violated any of the requirements, conditions, or prohibitions of this 
Chapter. A fine shall be imposed in the maximum amounts set forth in subsection (b) of this section upon 
findings made by the Director that the Tobacco Retailer, or any agent or employee of the Tobacco 
Retailer, has Sold any Tobacco Product to any Person(s) under the age of 21 years. Any administrative fine 
shall be imposed solely against the Tobacco Retailer, not the Tobacco Retailer’s employees or agents.
(b) Amount of Fine. Upon written findings made by the Director under subsection (a), the person or 
entity holding the Tobacco Retailer Permit shall be subject to an administrative fine for each such violation as 
follows:
(1) A fine not exceeding five hundred dollars ($500) for a first violation within a sixty (60) 
month period; and
(2) A fine not exceeding one thousand dollars ($1,000) for each subsequent violation within 
a sixty (60) month period.
(c) Each day that Tobacco Products are Sold or offered for Sale without a Permit or otherwise in 
violation of this Chapter shall constitute a separate violation. A finding of "offered for Sale" in violation of 
this Chapter will be made if Tobacco Products are either actually Sold and/or displayed in the retail 
establishment, or if advertisements offering to Sell Tobacco Products are visible to customers.
(d) Fine Procedures. Notice of the fine shall be served on the Tobacco Retailer by certified mail. The 
notice shall contain a description of the facts upon which the asserted violation is based and an advisement 
of the right to request a hearing before the Director contesting the imposition of the fine. Said hearing 
must be requested within ten calendar days of the date appearing on the notice of the fine. The decision of 
the Director shall be a final administrative order, with no administrative right of appeal.
(e) Failure to Pay Fine. If a fine imposed pursuant to this Chapter is not paid within 30 calendar days 
from the date appearing on the notice of the fine or of the notice of determination of the Director after 
the review provided for under subdivision (c) of this Section, the fine may be referred to a collection 
agency within or external to the County. In addition, any outstanding fines must be paid prior to the 
issuance of any new Permit or renewal of a Permit.

SUBJECT:
2nd & El Camino Real Garage Improvements – Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Award an agreement to MBH Architects, Inc. for design professional services in the amount of $570,641; establish a 
contingency reserve in the amount of $57,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in 
substantially the form presented and issue change orders within the contingency amount. 
BACKGROUND:
The 2nd & El Camino Real Garage has served the San Mateo downtown community for over seventy-five years. It is a 
concrete structure that has 385 parking spaces spanning five and a half stories. In 2021, a visual assessment identified 
multiple areas that are out of ADA compliance such as the slope along the path of travel, stairs, transitions, and lighting. 
The concrete façade panel connections were observed to be either broken or deteriorated. There are broken or missing 
concrete wheel stops, damaged vehicle barriers, corroded tube steel lintels, missing waterproofing at all structural joints, 
concrete cracking and spalling throughout, faded striping and missing wayfinding indicators. In 2022, ZFA Structural 
Engineering (ZFA) performed a structural investigation which identified exposed, ruptured, and corroded post-tension 
beam tendons in various areas and recommends that repairs be made in advance to restore the integrity of the structure. 
In February 2023, the Public Works Facilities Division interviewed three firms: Bureau Veritas; Edgett Williams Consulting 
Group; and MBH Architects, Inc. (MBH) to provide design professional services for this project.  Staff determined that MBH  
understood the scope and phasing for the project, has previous experience with the project’s structural engineer, and is 
able to guide the project to completion within the desired time frame.
On August 4, 2023, MBH submitted a proposal to produce construction documents for a two phased approach: Phase 1: 
Structural Repair and Phase 2: Parking Garage Improvements. These documents will include information required for 
permitting and construction that will be procured through the Job Order Contracting (JOC) process. Construction for Phase 
1 is planned for early-2024 and Phase 2 in mid-2024. 
Staff recommends approving this agreement in accordance with SMMC 3.60.040(c) which allows award to professional 
services consultants through a negotiated process without competitive bidding. Given MBH’s positive performance with 
similar projects in surrounding jurisdictions, their in-depth knowledge of this specific facility and their immediate 
availability, they are in the best position to perform this work. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is sufficient funding available in the Parking Facility Structural Repairs (46F025) project to award this agreement.

name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and 
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.

MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE

advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate 
limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or 
the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONSULTANT has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and 
shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.

SUBJECT:
2nd & El Camino Real and Central Parking Garages Elevator Controls Upgrade – Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with Consolidated CM, Inc. for elevator controls upgrade professional services in an amount not to 
exceed $147,950; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $15,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to 
execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and issue change orders within the contingency amount. 
BACKGROUND:
The elevator at the 2nd & El Camino Garage was installed in 1991 and serves five floors.  The elevator at Central Parking 
Garage was installed in 1999 and serves four floors.  Both elevators currently experience reliability issues and are at times 
out of service as they operate on obsolete control systems.  An assessment performed in 2018 recommended that a 
controls upgrade be implemented at both locations to maintain safe operations (“Project”). Design specifications were 
produced for both locations in 2023. Construction at the 2nd & El Camino Garage will begin in October 2023.  Construction 
at the Central Garage is planned for award and construction in the Spring of 2024.
The Project will require assistance for construction management and other professional services.  Facilities staff inquired 
with various types of construction management firms in the Bay Area and discovered that only one firm, Consolidated CM, 
Inc. (Consolidated), specializes in elevator control installations.  On August 2, 2023, Consolidated submitted a proposal on 
to provide construction management and support services for both locations.
Staff recommends approving this agreement in accordance with SMMC 3.60.040(c) which allows award to professional 
services consultants through a negotiated process without competitive bidding. Given that Consolidated specializes in 
elevator control installations, has a positive performance with similar projects in surrounding jurisdictions, and their in-
depth knowledge of these specific facilities, they are in the best position to perform this work. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is sufficient funding available in the Elevator Modernization Projects (461001 & 46F035) for this project. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation, repair, 
maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, facilities, 
mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 
15301.)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate 
limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or 
the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONSULTANT has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and 
shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.

City Council
FROM:
Alex Khojikian, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
September 05, 2023 
SUBJECT:
Alameda de las Pulgas Corridor Analysis and Hillsdale Boulevard at Alameda de las Pulgas Traffic Signal Design – 
Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with Sandis Civil Engineers Surveyors Planners for the Alameda de las Pulgas Corridor Analysis and 
Hillsdale Boulevard at Alameda de las Pulgas Traffic Signal Design project in the amount of $219,598; establish a 
contingency reserve in the amount of $22,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in 
substantially the form presented and issue change orders within the contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
In 2017, a traffic signal was requested at the Hillsdale Boulevard at Alameda de las Pulgas intersection through the 
Hillsdale/Beresford Traffic Action Plan. In 2018, staff conducted a signal warrant analysis and found that the intersection 
meets the eight-hour and four-hour warrants, meaning that the proposed traffic signal improvements at the subject 
intersection are justified per California Manual on Uniform Traffic Control Devices standards. 
The adopted 2020 Bicycle Master Plan identifies a proposed Class II bike lane on Alameda de las Pulgas; as that project is 
not yet funded for design, staff has scoped a corridor traffic analysis as part of this project that will look to assess current 
and future roadway operations on Alameda de las Pulgas to support future bicycle project implementation. The corridor 
traffic analysis will also produce high-level operational scopes for potential future traffic signal projects at the intersections 
of 28th, 31st, and 36th Avenues along the subject corridor. The proposed traffic signal operations at Hillsdale Boulevard 
and Alameda de las Pulgas intersection will look to optimize safety for all modes of transportation and work towards 
minimizing current and future operational deficiencies along the Alameda de las Pulgas corridor.
Sandis Civil Engineers Surveyors Planners (Sandis) was selected through a qualification process using a request for 
proposals (RFP) for professional engineering design services. The project was advertised on May 23, 2023, and a total of 
seven (7) proposals were received on June 21, 2023. Staff reviewed the seven proposals and short-listed three (3) 
consultants for interviews that were held on July 17, 2023. Of the three consultants that were interviewed, Sandis’ 
proposed scope, schedule, and budget best align with the City’s needs. Therefore, staff recommends awarding an 
agreement with Sandis to perform the design services for this project for an amount not to exceed $219,598 and establish 
a contingency reserve of $22,000 (10% of the contract budget) to cover any unforeseen changes during the design process.
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is sufficient funding in the Hillsdale Boulevard and Alameda de las Pulgas Signal (46R001) project account to award 
this agreement as well as the contingency reserve.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This project is exempt from CEQA review as an “existing facility,” in that the traffic signal installation project consists of the 
operation, repair, maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, 
facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features involving  negligible or no expansion of existing or former use. 
(CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.)

and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.

testimony, testimony, and travel at CONSULTANT's standard hourly rates at the time of actual 
testimony.

PROJECT COORDINATION AND PROJECT 
MANAGEMENT
Upon NTP, our team will schedule a kick off meeting to establish 
lines of communication with City staff to discuss scope of work, 
schedule, and budget. We will also request and compile available 
information from the City ahead of develop- ing a Detailed Work 
Plan to confirm alignment with the City’s goals for the project.
We will meet with City staff regularly and will provide project 
management services, including meeting agendas and notes, 
maintaining the project schedule and budget, invoices, and 
regular communication with the City.
Deliverables:
•
Scope of work
•
Schedule
•
Budget
•
Information request
CORRIDOR TRAFFIC ANALYSIS
Our Traffic Team, led by Alta and supported by Kittelson, will 
analyze traffic operations along Alameda de las Pulgas between 
24th Avenue and 42nd Avenue to ultimately evaluate the 
implementation of bike facilities recommended in the City’s 2020 
Bicycle Master Plan.
To do so, our team will acquire traffic counts from a traffic count 
vendor for the AM and PM 2-Hour peak period pedes- trian, 
bicycle, and vehicle turning movement counts at the following 
intersections (or as otherwise decided):
•
Alameda de Las Pulgas and 28th Avenue
•
Alameda de Las Pulgas and Ventura Avenue
•
Alameda de Las Pulgas and 29th Avenue
•
Alameda de Las Pulgas and Terrace Way
•
Alameda de Las Pulgas and 30th Avenue
•
Alameda de Las Pulgas and Sylvan Avenue
•
Alameda de Las Pulgas and 31st Avenue
•
Alameda de Las Pulgas and Ander Lane
•
Alameda de Las Pulgas and Heather Lane
•
Alameda de Las Pulgas and Stephen Road
•
Alameda de Las Pulgas and West Hillsdale Boulevard
•
Alameda de Las Pulgas and Voelker Drive
•
Alameda de Las Pulgas and 36th Avenue
All counts shall be collected between the weekdays of Tues- day 
through Thursday.
Alta will provide a data request form to the City for all available 
traffic signal data (phasing, signal timing and signal coordi- 
nation), historic traffic counts and planned future projects that 
may affect the traffic operations along the corridor. Alta will 
review the traffic count data received to ensure the most 
relevant counts are incorporated into the analysis. Should it be 
deemed necessary, Alta will also include any requests for the 
City’s Streetlight Data and Remix by Via subscriptions in this 
initial data request.
TRAVEL DEMAND FORECASTS
Kittelson will prepare travel demand forecasts for the Alameda 
de Las Pulgas corridor from 24th Avenue to 42nd Avenue, and the 
portion of Hillsdale Boulevard crossing the study corridor.  
Kittelson will use the current citywide travel model developed by 
Kittelson as part of the general plan update. Kittelson will then 
extract forecasts for several scenarios, providing segment and 
intersection-level forecasts for further Synchro LOS processing 
by the Team.  This will start with 2019 base year model and add 
recent new facilities that opened (including grade crossings at 
28th and 31st Avenues at ECR). Kittelson will then conduct a brief 
localized validation check using the 2023 counts.  We propose to 
use the 2040 Preferred land use scenario for the cumulative 
2040 modeling as it represents the likely buildout of the city’s 
general plan. 
Our Team will collect new counts during the September period 
that Kittelson will use to validate the base year model in the 
corridor and increment the growth forecast.  
We propose to provide traffic forecasts at up to 6 intersections, 
as follows:
1.
ADLP/28th Avenue
2.
ADLP/31st Avenue
3.
ADLP/Hillsdale Avenue
4.
ADLP/36th Avenue
5.
TBD (if required)
6.
TBD (if required)
And up to 4 scenarios, but may include:
1.
2019/23 no-build (for model validation)
2.
2019/23 reduced lane + bike lane extension
3.
2040 no-build
4.
2040 reduced lane + bike lane extension
Should it be necessary, Kittelson anticipates the team would 
utilize the forecasts from these four scenarios to manually fit any 
other operational scenarios that need testing.

--- page 113 ---

S  C  O P E

CITY OF SAN MATEO ALAMEDA DE LAS PULGAS CORRIDOR ANALYSIS AND HILLSDALE BOULEVARD AT

SANDIS.NET 3
Kittleson will run the citywide model and extract the following 
outputs for the team:
1.
Processed intersection peak hour turn volumes at all 
study intersections (in Excel).
2.
Select link runs on ALDP and Hillsdale to assist the team 
with quantifying the percent local vs regional cut-
through traffic (intent is to demonstrate how much 
traffic could potentially divert as a result of a lane 
reduction associated with the bike lane extension 
scenarios).   
We anticipate the team will review the volume demands with 
the City to determine if they reasonably represent the growth 
and change in demands associated with the lane reduction, new 
signal, and bike lane addition scenarios. Following the review, if 
needed, the team can opt to make manual adjustments based 
on engineering judgment, especially to left turn volumes which 
may influence traffic signal timing and queue lengths.
We will not extract VMT results since there is no CEQA analysis 
for this project. However, should the City request it, additional 
performance measures can be extracted in the study area for 
community engagement.
EXISTING AND FUTURE CONDITIONS ANALYSES
Alta will perform the intersection traffic operations analysis 
based on count data collected/received to determine the average 
queue length and average vehicle delay during the AM and PM 
peak periods.
This analysis will utilize existing traffic volumes only to study 
the existing and future conditions with and without the 
planned bikeway improvements with one proposed roadway 
configuration for the planned bikeway at the project 
intersections identified above. The conditions will be evaluated 
in the existing and future scenarios. The Alta team will use 
Synchro (v11) software, the accompanying SimTraffic software, 
and Highway Capacity Manual (HCM) 6th Edition methodologies 
for estimating vehicle delays and queue lengths. Anticipated 
queue lengths will be reported for each intersection approach, 
and reported delay shall be represented as average vehicle 
delay per intersection for each scenario analyzed. The 
scenarios developed will be the following:
•
Existing Conditions (2023) without Planned Bikeway 
Improvements
•
Existing Conditions (2023) with Planned Bikeway 
Improvements
•
Future Conditions (2040) without Planned Bikeway 
Improvements
•
Future Conditions (2040) with Planned Bikeway 
Improvements
The proposed configuration for the Existing and Future 
Conditions with the Planned Bikeway Improvements shall include 
a road diet along Alameda de las Pulgas, which shall remove one 
travel lane in each direction. The Existing and Future Conditions 
with the Planned Bikeway Improvements shall also include high-
level intersection design and operations, which may include, but 
are not limited to, turn pockets, parking removal, bicycle and 
pedestrian phasing, signal timing improvements, striping 
improvements, and hardscape improvements.
These improvements shall be identified and proposed for the 
optimization of safety and comfort for all users and work 
towards minimizing operational deficiencies.
In order for the future conditions to be analyzed, Alta will utilize 
the traffic forecasting completed by Kittelson. 
The analysis shall also assess changes in volume to capacity 
(V/C) ratios for each of the identified scenarios and shall include 
high level operations scopes for traffic signals at the project and 
for Alameda de las Pulgas at 28th, 31st, and 36th Avenue 
intersections and up to two additional locations, for future 
conditions.
ALTERNATIVE CONCEPTS AND ANALYSIS
HILLSDALE BOULEVARD AT ALAMEDA DE LAS PULGAS INTERSECTION
Special considerations will be given to the intersection of Alameda 
de las Pulgas and Hillsdale Boulevard, understanding- ing that the 
installation of the traffic signal will precede the implementation of 
the bicycle facilities on Alameda de las Pulgas. As such, high-level 
alternative concept designs will be produced for this intersection. 
Up to three alternative designs may be produced, in AutoCAD and 
on aerial imagery at 1”=20’ scale. Each alternative will provide 
means for the bicycle facilities to be implemented at the 
intersection while mini- mizing the amount of work to be 
completed on the new traffic signal equipment for the facilities to 
be compatible. This work will account for additional signal heads 
that may be required for the bicycle facility phasing, the changing 
alignment of lanes approaching the intersection and their 
relationship to signal equipment placement and any phasing 
changes that may be required for the bicycle facility 
implementation. These alternative designs will not require the 
addition of new poles or mast arms for the bicycle facilities to be 
implemented.
Each alternative shall be assessed for its connectivity, safety, and 
operational opportunities and trade-offs that it presents for the 
various modes of users. This will include a LOS delay, queuing, and 
volume to capacity ratio analysis for each alter-

native in the Existing Conditions.
This alternatives comparison shall be presented to the

PREFERRED ALTERNATIVE AND ANALYSIS MEMORANDUM
Alta will provide the City with a draft traffic study memoran- dum 
for review. The City may provide a response in the form of 
consolidated, consistent comments on the memorandum. Alta 
will address the comments and provide a final traffic study 
memorandum. This memorandum will outline the preferred 
design, which shall include the preferred alternative for the 
design of Alameda de las Pulgas and Hillsborough Boulevard 
after receiving public input. It will also identify the necessary 
signal modifications, if any, for the implementation of the bicycle 
facilities at this intersection.
Both submittals will be accompanied with appendices, which 
will include, but is not limited to, the collected traffic data, all 
Synchro output reports from the Synchro analysis, and all 
SimTraffic queueing reports from the queuing analysis.

High-level operations phasing for traffic signals at

Final Design and operations memorandum for Hillsdale

STAKEHOLDER AND COMMUNITY ENGAGEMENT
COMMUNITY OUTREACH PLAN
Alta will work closely with the City of San Mateo to develop a 
Community Engagement Plan (CEP) that will outline the 
strategies and resources to be used to meaningfully engage
with the community and various stakeholders, including those 
who are typically difficult to reach. The CEP will also include
a schedule of activities, deliverables, and anticipated actions 
required of the City. We are sensitive to the limits on par- 
ticipants’ time, and will structure outreach and engagement 
opportunities that align with existing meetings and events as 
much as possible.
We anticipate that the CEP will also include a list of organiza- 
tions and contacts at Equity Priority Communities and CBOs to 
focus on and ensure that these communities achieve equitable 
access to safe active transportation.
WEBSITE (VIRTUAL OPEN HOUSE)
Alta will develop virtual workshops where participants can evaluate 
scenarios using slider photo renderings to show existing and 
future alternative cross-sections of real locations on the corridor 
along with benefits and trade-offs for each alternative. The virtual 
workshop will record participant input and collect ranked priorities 
on each alternative. A hard copy version will be available to collect 
input for mobile workshops.
Alta proposes to design and develop a custom web- based virtual 
open house for this project (an example can be seen at 
https://grandave.altaplanning.cloud/), starting from content 
strategy and mockups, incorporating interactive map ele- ments, 
contextual project details, narrative copy, and support- ing text 
and infographics. The virtual open house will allow the general 
public to learn about the project’s extents, the current facilities, 
and proposed alternative typologies. The virtual open house will 
also afford the public opportunities to provide feedback during 
each phase of the project. Public input data will be collected 
anonymously and stored privately for export and analysis 
periodically during the active public commenting period as 
needed, and as a final export at the close of the commenting 
period.
CONTENT STRATEGY
Alta will work with the City to determine overall strategies and 
goals, content priorities, and other functional details needed 
through a virtual open house questionnaire. Alta will assess 
graphic asset and data needs and availability based on client 
guidance received through the questionnaire, and provide the 
City with a content inventory, listing content (text, high resolution 
photos, data, and graphic assets) needed to procure or produce 
prior to launch. Using the answers from the questionnaire, Alta 
will produce a draft storyboard and wireframes for two phases of 
the virtual open house for the City’s review and approval. These 
will establish a strategy
and structure for the virtual open house before any mockup 
design begins, and help with outlining and determining 
functional elements, organizing and prioritizing content, and 
planning design direction. 
The City will review the storyboard and wireframes and provide 
Alta with a consolidated, non-contradictory set of comments to 
incorporate into the design mockups.
CONTENT DEVELOPMENT

subsequent round.
VIRTUAL OPEN HOUSE WEB DEVELOPMENT
With the client’s approval of the design mockups, Alta will 
proceed with production of the first development draft of the 
first phase of the virtual open house, which will include all 
design and content elements established through the content 
strategy and mockup processes. Depending on the functional 
details established during the content strategy process, some 
features or functionality may not be present or subject to 
review until the second round, and the first development draft 
will not be fully mobile optimized. This task includes two rounds 
of review (one draft, one final) for each of the three phases of 
the virtual open house. For each round in each phase, the City 
will review the development draft and provide Alta with a single, 
consolidated, non-contradictory set of comments to respond to 
or address in the subsequent round.
The final developed version will be feature-complete, mobile 
optimized, and accessible as defined by the WCAG 2.0 guide- 
lines. Alta will privately host the development draft of the virtual 
open house throughout the development process, providing 
access to the City during each scheduled review period to 
facilitate review, testing, and feedback. This development and 
review process will repeat for each of the three phases of the 
virtual open house. After the initial phase launches, subsequent 
development and review will take place on a separate preview 
instance of the virtual open house, with the final approved 
version deployed to replace the previous version at an agreed-
upon launch date for each phase.
FINAL LAUNCH
Leading up to the public launch of the first phase, Alta will, if 
necessary, coordinate with the City to acquire a unique
domain name for the virtual open house. Alta will be responsi- ble 
for technical administration of the new or existing domain name 
for the public launch, and will continue to provide host- ing of the 
virtual open house in its public production envi- ronment for one 
year for a fixed fee of $2,000. No changes, updates, or 
maintenance after the public launch are included in this scope. 
After one year, Alta will privately archive the virtual open house, 
cancel any domain names associated with it, and provide a 
packaged archive of the virtual open house to the City upon 
request.
DEVELOPMENT OF COLLATERAL MATERIALS
Alta will create and print marketing collateral that includes project 
flyers, A-frame poster boards, postcards or door hangers for 
businesses and residents, cards to leave on wind- shields and bike 
spokes.
OUTREACH ACTIVITIES
Alta will work with the City to provide an inclusive, iterative and 
comprehensive suite of outreach activities. Outreach events will 
focus on gathering input from the community on opportunities 
and challenges related to the design concepts. Proposed events 
include:
•
Stakeholder interviews – up to three (3 stakeholder inter- 
views). It is anticipated that the City will lead all logistical 
considerations for these meetings.

1 project workshop– potential location TBD
•
Development of Postcard mailers with notices about the 
meetings and explanations about the project to neighbors 
within ½ mile buffer of project
•
Attendance of up to one Sustainability and infrastructure 
commission meeting (up to 1 staff; 3 hrs)
SUMMARY OF ENGAGEMENT
Alta will take the collected outreach materials and results from 
the above tasks and develop a graphical outreach sum- mary 
memo for incorporation into the final plan. The summary will 
feature maps of identified issues, high-level summary analyses, 
and photos from events. Comment card comments will be 
compiled into a Microsoft Excel matrix for SCTA to use.

HILLSDALE BOULEVARD AT ALAMEDA DE LAS 
PULGAS TRAFFIC SIGNAL PLANS, 
SPECIFICATIONS, AND ESTIMATE (PS&E)
Upon kickoff of this task, a detailed work plan and schedule will 
be developed by Sandis to complete the PS&E phase in- cluding 
an outline of the various tasks and submittal delivery dates 
necessary to complete the PS&E and bid the project.
The PS&E phase will consist of the following submittals:
•
35% (Plans)
•
65% (Plans, Draft Specifications, and Estimate)
•
95% (Plans, Specifications, and Estimate/Bid List)
•
100% Final (Plans, Specifications, and Estimate/Bid List)
We assume that 20 working days are needed for City review of 
35% and 65% submittals and 15 working days for City review of all 
other submittals. Comments will be provided in a single 
consolidated set of redlines. Our team will also be available to 
attend plan review “page turners” if needed, to expedite plan 
review.
The City will submit a PG&E service application within two weeks 
following review, revision, and resubmittal of 35% plans. Sandis 
suggests the City review and consider submitting the application 
upon selecting the preferred signal layout in the previous task; 
our team can propose a suitable location for the service cabinet 
so that the application may be reviewed and submitted.
The design plan set will include infrastructure and equipment 
necessary to operate the traffic signal as identified in the pre- 
ferred scenario selected in the prior phase. This may include but 
is not limited to signal poles and mast arms, detection
for all modes, emergency vehicle preemption, CCTV, com- 
munications to the nearest online intersection, traffic signal 
cabinet and contents, conduits, conductors, phase diagrams, and 
lighting. The plan set will also include necessary civil engineering 
work needed to implement the signal operations identified in the 
preferred scenario, including but not limited to, median cutback 
and concrete restoration, pavement resto- ration, pedestrian 
ramps, and new and replaced landscaping. We assume that utility 
and landscaping improvements are minimal; further 
improvements can be provided as an additional service. 
Our plan set will also include design detail for drainage im- pacts 
and sufficient utility information to satisfy the project’s utility 
certification. It should be noted that the example signal plan 
provided was from San Clemente and utilizes a conductor 
schedule formatting that is typical for Southern California. Our 
team is well experienced with this format but recommends a 
more typical conductor schedule to Northern California to attract 
competitive bids.
TOPOGRAPHICAL SURVEY AND BASE MAPPING
Sandis will perform a topographic field survey to gather the 
necessary information and detail for the design of the Project at 
the intersection of W. Hillsdale Blvd and Alameda de las Pulgas. 
The boundary shall establish City right-of-way and be used to 
confirm that all improvements are within the City’s right-of-way.
Existing right-of-way will be based upon available maps and deeds 
on file in the County public records. We will include and show 
plottable easements, if any, and right-of-way lines with length and 
bearing (including reference on basis) on each boundary course. A 
Preliminary Title Report with referenced documents will be 
ordered if needed.
Sandis will conduct fieldwork, office calculations, and drafting to 
produce a topographic survey of the project area at an a
1” = 20’ Scale. This survey will show the location and sizes of 
existing trees (Driplines will be assumed), grade breaks, high 
points, low points signs, fences, walls, buildings, striping, 
driveways, walkways, drainages, structures, lights, poles, 
bollards, vegetated or landscaped areas (including bushes, etc), 
USA markings, vaults, valves, meters, boxes, pedestals, cleanouts, 
manholes, drain inlets, catch basins, culverts, out- falls, and 
standpipes within the project area(s). Field measure- ments of 
inverts of accessible and unobstructed visible catch basins, area 
drains, storm drain manholes, and sanitary sewer manholes will 
be shown.
Elevation spot grades and/or the combination of contours will be 
shown at one (1) foot intervals or as appropriate to clearly define 
the slopes. Elevations collected by ground surveys will be shown 
to an accuracy of 0.01’ (one hundredth) of a foot.
Heavily brushed areas will be defined at the perimeter. Brush 
clearing will be the responsibility of the client if ground eleva- 
tions need to be collected in those areas. Existing elevations shall 
be shown at a maximum of 100-foot cross sections. Spot 
elevations shall be shown at all points of vertical or horizontal 
change (grade break). Elevations will be based on available NGS 
or locally published benchmarks. Utility information will be based 
on surface evidence located in the field and the solicitation of the 
records of the various utility providers. Sandis will coordinate 
directly with the utility providers to achieve this. Sandis will issue 
an underground service alert to field-verify the data provided by 
various utilities, particularly where there may be conflicts with 
proposed pole and conduit locations.
Mechanical detection and/or potholing (up to eight) of existing 
high risk utilities will also be provided.

EXHIBIT C 
 
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS 
 
 
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE  
Coverage shall be at least as broad as: 
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate limit 
applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or the 
general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit. 
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if CONSULTANT 
has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no less than 
$1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage. 
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury 
or disease.  
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate 
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and shall 
be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT. 
Other Insurance Provisions 
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions: 
Additional Insured Status 
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used). 
Primary Coverage 
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it. 
Notice of Cancellation 
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City. 
121 of 265

--- page 122 ---
Design Professional Services 2022 
 
Page 10 of 10 
Rev 9/22 
Waiver of Subrogation 
CONSULTANT hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said 
CONSULTANT may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  
CONSULTANT agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of 
subrogation, but this provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of 
subrogation endorsement from the insurer.   
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions 
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the CONSULTANT to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof 
of ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within 
the retention.   
Acceptability of Insurers 
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless 
otherwise acceptable to the City. 
Verification of Coverage 
CONSULTANT shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies 
of the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause.  All certificates and 
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure 
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the CONSULTANT’s 
obligation to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

SUBJECT:
On-Call Professional Consultant Services – Agreements
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve individual on-call professional consultant services agreements each for a term through December 31, 2025 with: 
Geocon Consultants, Inc. in an amount not to exceed $250,000; Sandis Civil Engineering Surveyors Planners in an amount 
not to exceed $300,000; Ghirardelli Associates, Inc. in an amount not to exceed $300,000; Park Engineering, Inc. in an 
amount not to exceed $300,000; BSK Associates in an amount not to exceed $150,000; and Nichols Consulting Engineers, 
CHTD. in an amount not to exceed $150,000; and Authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreements in 
substantially the form presented and any future no-cost amendments. 
BACKGROUND:
On January 20, 2023, the Department of Public Works staff issued a request for proposals (RFP) to select qualified firms to 
provide on-call professional consulting services for various specializations, including geotechnical services, surveying 
services, construction management and inspection, material testing, environmental and environmental compliance 
services, and potholing and underground facility locating. Consultant services are needed to assist the City in managing 
and implementing capital improvement projects. 
The City received a total of thirty-eight (38) proposals that were evaluated based on the firms’ project understanding, 
experience with similar projects, and technical ability of key staff. The on-call engineering consulting firms recommended 
by staff for each specialization are in the table below, along with respective recommended agreement amounts. The not to 
exceed contract amounts for each consultant are based upon the type of services to be delivered and the estimated level 
of effort needed for these services.
Consultant
Service
Award Amount Not to Exceed
Geocon Consultants
Geotechnical 
$250,000
Sandis Civil Engineers Surveyors and Planners
Surveying, Potholing & Underground Facility 
Locating
$300,000
Ghirardelli Associates
Construction Management & Inspection
$300,000
Park Engineering
Construction Management & Inspection
$300,000
BSK Associates
Material Testing
$150,000
Nichols Consulting Engineers
Environmental & Environmental Compliance
$150,000
The proposed term of the agreements are through December 31, 2025, unless amended. Staff will develop specific project 
task orders, scopes of work, and budgets with each firm for work efforts performed as part of the on-call services.  Based 
on the above, staff recommends that Council approve the on-call agreements.

Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)

AGREEMENT WITH GEOCON CONSULTANTS, INC.
FOR PROFESSIONAL ON CALL CONSULTANT SERVICES
FOR 
GEOTECHNICAL SERVICES
This Agreement, made and entered into this day of ____________________, by and between 
the CITY OF SAN MATEO, a municipal corporation existing under the laws of the State of California 
(“CITY”), and Geocon Consultants, Inc., a corporation (“CONSULTANT” or “Geocon”), with offices at 
6671 Brisa Street, Livermore, CA 94550.
RECITALS:
A.  CITY desires certain on call geotechnical services hereinafter described.
B.  CITY desires to engage CONSULTANT to provide these on call geotechnical services by 
reason of its qualifications and experience for performing such services and CONSULTANT has offered 
to provide the required services on the terms and in the manner set forth herein.
NOW, THEREFORE, IT IS AGREED as follows:
SECTION 1 - SCOPE OF SERVICES
The scope of services to be performed by CONSULTANT under this Agreement is as described in 
Exhibit A to this Agreement, attached and incorporated by reference.
SECTION 2 - DUTIES OF CONSULTANT
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for the professional quality, technical accuracy and 
coordination of all work furnished by CONSULTANT under this Agreement.  CONSULTANT shall, without 
additional compensation, correct or revise any errors or deficiencies in its work.
CONSULTANT represents that it is qualified to furnish the services described under this 
Agreement.
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for employing or engaging all persons necessary to perform 
the services of CONSULTANT.
CONSULTANT agrees to comply with the City’s minimum wage ordinance as codified in 
Municipal Code Chapter 5.92, which differs from the state minimum wage and includes a Consumer 
Price Index escalator.
CONSULTANT and his subconsultants shall comply with State’s Prevailing Wage Laws.

--- page 126 ---
Professional Services
Page 2 of 12
Rev 9/22
SECTION 3 - DUTIES OF CITY
CITY shall provide pertinent information regarding its requirements for the project.
CITY shall examine documents submitted by CONSULTANT and shall render decisions pertaining 
thereto promptly, to avoid unreasonable delay in the progress of CONSULTANT's work.
SECTION 4 - TERM
The services to be performed under this Agreement shall commence on upon execution of this 
agreement and be completed on December 31, 2025. This term of this Agreement may be extended by 
written amendment executed by the Director of Public Works and a duly authorized representative of 
CONSULTANT.
SECTION 5 - PAYMENT
Payment shall be made by CITY only for services rendered and upon submission of a payment 
request upon completion and CITY approval of the work performed.  In consideration for the full 
performance of the services set forth in Exhibit A, CITY agrees to pay CONSULTANT a fee, based on 
verified time and materials, in an amount of $250,000, pursuant to rates stated in Exhibit B to this 
Agreement, attached and incorporated by reference.
Cost adjustment for the second and subsequent year’s annual fixed amounts will be made using 
annual indexes of the “Consumer Price Index for All Urban Consumers,” Bay Area City Average, all 
items (1967=100) as published in the Monthly Review by the U.S. Department of Labor, (CPI). The 
annual increase in rates is not to exceed CPI or 3%, whichever is lower.
SECTION 6 - TERMINATION
Without limitation to such rights or remedies as CITY shall otherwise have by law, CITY shall have 
the right to terminate this Agreement or suspend work on the Project for any reason, upon ten (10) days' 
written notice to CONSULTANT.  CONSULTANT agrees to cease all work under this Agreement upon 
receipt of said written notice.
Upon termination and upon CITY's payment of the amount required to be paid, documents 
become the property of CITY, and CONSULTANT shall transfer them to CITY upon request without 
additional compensation.
SECTION 7 - OWNERSHIP OF DOCUMENTS
All documents prepared by CONSULTANT in the performance of this Agreement, although 
instruments of professional service, are and shall be the property of CITY, whether the project for 
which they are made is executed or not.
