SECTION 8 - CONFIDENTIALITY
All reports and documents prepared by CONSULTANT in connection with the performance of 
this Agreement are confidential until released by CITY to the public.  CONSULTANT shall not make any 
such documents or information available to any individual or organization not employed by 
CONSULTANT or CITY without the written consent of CITY before any such release.
SECTION 9 - INTEREST OF CONSULTANT
CONSULTANT covenants that it presently has no interest, and shall not acquire any interest, 
direct or indirect, financial or otherwise, which would conflict in any manner or degree with the 
performance of the services under this Agreement.
SECTION 10 - CONSULTANT'S STATUS
It is expressly agreed that in the performance of the professional services required under this 
Agreement, CONSULTANT shall at all times be considered an independent contractor as defined in 
Labor Code Section 3353, under control of the CITY as to the result of the work but not the means by 
which the result is accomplished.  Nothing herein shall be construed to make CONSULTANT an agent or 
employee of CITY while providing services under this Agreement.
SECTION 11 - INDEMNITY
CONSULTANT agrees to hold harmless and indemnify CITY, its elected and appointed officials, 
employees, and agents from and against any and all claims, loss, liability, damage, and expense arising 
out of CONSULTANT’s performance of this Agreement, except those claims arising out of CITY’s sole 
negligence or willful misconduct.  CONSULTANT agrees to defend City, its elected and appointed 
officials, employees, and agents against any such claims. The CONSULTANT’S duty to indemnify shall 
survive expiration or early termination of this Agreement.
SECTION 12 - INSURANCE
CONSULTANT shall procure and maintain for the duration of the contract and three years 
thereafter (five years for building or major improvements) the insurance specified in Exhibit C to this 
Agreement.
SECTION 13 - NON-ASSIGNABILITY
Both parties hereto recognize that this Agreement is for the personal services of CONSULTANT 
and cannot be transferred, assigned, or subcontracted by CONSULTANT without the prior written 
consent of CITY.

SECTION 14 - RELIANCE UPON PROFESSIONAL
SKILL OF CONSULTANT
It is mutually understood and agreed by and between the parties hereto that CONSULTANT is 
skilled in the professional calling necessary to perform the work agreed to be done under this 
Agreement and that CITY relies upon the skill of CONSULTANT to do and perform the work with the 
care and skill ordinarily used by members of CONSULTANT’s profession practicing under the same or 
similar circumstances at the same locality, and CONSULTANT agrees to thus perform the work. The 
acceptance of CONSULTANT's work by CITY does not operate as a release of CONSULTANT from said 
obligation. 
SECTION 15 - WAIVERS
The waiver by either party of any breach or violation of any term, covenant, or condition of this 
Agreement or of any provisions of any ordinance or law shall not be deemed to be a waiver of such 
term, covenant, condition, ordinance or law or of any subsequent breach or violation of the same or of 
any other term, condition, ordinance, or law.  The subsequent acceptance by either party of any fee or 
other money which may become due hereunder shall not be deemed to be a waiver of any preceding 
breach or violation by the other party of any term, covenant, or condition of this Agreement or of any 
applicable law or ordinance.
SECTION 16 - SEVERABILITY
If any term or portion of this Agreement is held to be invalid, illegal, or otherwise 
unenforceable by a court of competent jurisdiction, the remaining provisions of this Agreement shall 
continue in full force and effect.
SECTION 17 - COSTS AND ATTORNEY FEES
Attorney fees in total amount not exceeding $5000, shall be recoverable as costs (by the filing 
of a cost bill) by the prevailing party in any action or actions to enforce the provisions of this 
Agreement.  The above $5000 limit is the total of attorney fees recoverable whether in the trial court, 
appellate court, or otherwise, and regardless of the number of attorneys, trials, appeals, or actions.  It 
is the intent of this Agreement that neither party shall have to pay the other more than $5000 for 
attorney fees arising out of an action, or actions to enforce the provisions of this Agreement.
SECTION 18 - NON-DISCRIMINATION
CONSULTANT warrants that it is an Equal Opportunity Employer and shall comply with 
applicable regulations governing equal employment opportunity.  Neither CONSULTANT nor any of its 
subcontractors shall discriminate in the employment of any person because of race, color, national 
origin, ancestry, physical handicap, medical condition, marital status, sex, or age, unless based upon a 
bona fide occupational qualification pursuant to the California Fair Employment and Housing Act.

SECTION 19 - MEDIATION
Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be submitted to 
mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be 
agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one 
name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and 
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.
SECTION 20 - LITIGATION
CONSULTANT shall testify at CITY'S request if litigation is brought against CITY in connection 
with CONSULTANT's services under this Agreement.  Unless the action is brought by CONSULTANT, or 
is based upon CONSULTANT's wrongdoing, CITY shall compensate CONSULTANT for preparation for 
testimony, testimony, and travel at CONSULTANT's standard hourly rates at the time of actual 
testimony.
SECTION 21 - NOTICES
All notices hereunder shall be given in writing and mailed, postage prepaid, addressed as

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
Service Tasks include but are not limited to:
1.
Pre-exploration activities & geotechnical feasibility assessment.
a.
Review of existing geotechnical data, public documentation, geologic maps, aerial 
photographs, and historic groundwater level.
b.
Permitting.
2.
Field exploration and geotechnical investigations.
a.
Soil sampling.
b.
Laboratory testing of select soil samples for moisture-density, Atterberg Limits, gradation, 
strength, corrosivity, consolidation tests, and R-value.
c.
Compiling and analyzing field and laboratory data.
3.
Initial and final design level geotechnical reports, detailing site conditions, constraints, any 
applicable mitigation measures, findings, data results, and recommendations.
4.
Supervision of all work by a registered Geotechnical Engineer (“GE”) and/or a Certified Engineering 
Geologist (“CEG”), as required.

EXHIBIT C
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate 
limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or 
the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONSULTANT has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and 
shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any CGL or Automobile Liability claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance 
coverage shall be primary insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, 
employees, and agents. Any CGL or Automobile Liability insurance or self-insurance maintained by the 
City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s 
insurance and shall not contribute with it.

Rev 9/22
Notice of Cancellation
CONSULTANT shall immediately notify the City when it has notice or receives notification that any 
insurance overage is subject to cancellation, or is in fact cancelled, lapsed, or otherwise unavailable.
Waiver of Subrogation
CONSULTANT hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said 
CONSULTANT may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  
CONSULTANT agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of 
subrogation, but this provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of 
subrogation endorsement from the insurer. Notwithstanding the foregoing with respect to
Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions) waiver of subrogation may be provided as required by
written contract per policy form in lieu of an endorsement page. 
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the CONSULTANT to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof 
of ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within 
the retention.  
Acceptability of Insurers
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless 
otherwise acceptable to the City.
Verification of Coverage
CONSULTANT shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies 
of the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause.  All certificates and 
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure 
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the CONSULTANT’s 
obligation to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

AGREEMENT WITH SANDIS CIVIL ENGINEERS SURVEYORS PLANNERS
FOR PROFESSIONAL ON CALL CONSULTANT SERVICES
FOR 
SURVEYING, POTHOLING, AND UNDERGROUND FACILITY LOCATING SERVICES
This Agreement, made and entered into this day of ____________________, by and between 
the CITY OF SAN MATEO, a municipal corporation existing under the laws of the State of California 
(“CITY”), and Sandis Civil Engineers Surveyors Planners, a corporation, (“CONSULTANT”), with offices at 
1700 S. Winchester Boulevard, Suite 200, Campbell, CA 95008.
RECITALS:
A.  CITY desires certain on-call surveying, potholing, and underground facility locating 
B.  CITY desires to engage CONSULTANT to provide these on-call surveying, potholing, 
and underground facility locating services by reason of its qualifications and experience for performing 
such services and CONSULTANT has offered to provide the required services on the terms and in the 
manner set forth herein.
NOW, THEREFORE, IT IS AGREED as follows:
SECTION 1 - SCOPE OF SERVICES
The scope of services to be performed by CONSULTANT under this Agreement is as described in 
Exhibit A to this Agreement, attached and incorporated by reference.
SECTION 2 - DUTIES OF CONSULTANT
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for the professional quality, technical accuracy and 
coordination of all work furnished by CONSULTANT under this Agreement.  CONSULTANT shall, without 
additional compensation, correct or revise any errors or deficiencies in its work.
CONSULTANT represents that it is qualified to furnish the services described under this 
Agreement.
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for employing or engaging all persons necessary to perform 
the services of CONSULTANT.
CONSULTANT agrees to comply with the City’s minimum wage ordinance as codified in 
Municipal Code Chapter 5.92, which differs from the state minimum wage and includes a Consumer 
Price Index escalator.
CONSULTANT and his subconsultants shall comply with State’s Prevailing Wage Laws.

--- page 138 ---

Page 2 of 12
Rev 9/22
SECTION 3 - DUTIES OF CITY
CITY shall provide pertinent information regarding its requirements for the project.
CITY shall examine documents submitted by CONSULTANT and shall render decisions pertaining 
thereto promptly, to avoid unreasonable delay in the progress of CONSULTANT's work.
SECTION 4 - TERM
The services to be performed under this Agreement shall commence upon execution of this 
agreement and be completed on December 31, 2025. This term of this Agreement may be extended by 
written amendment executed by the Director of Public Works and a duly authorized representative of 
CONSULTANT.
SECTION 5 - PAYMENT
Payment shall be made by CITY only for services rendered and upon submission of a payment 
request upon completion and CITY approval of the work performed.  In consideration for the full 
performance of the services set forth in Exhibit A, CITY agrees to pay CONSULTANT a fee, based on 
verified time and materials, in an amount of $300,000, pursuant to rates stated in Exhibit B to this 
Agreement, attached and incorporated by reference.
Cost adjustment for the second and subsequent year’s annual fixed amounts will be made using 
annual indexes of the “Consumer Price Index for All Urban Consumers,” Bay Area City Average, all 
items (1967=100) as published in the Monthly Review by the U.S. Department of Labor, (CPI). The 
annual increase in rates is not to exceed CPI or 3%, whichever is lower.
SECTION 6 - TERMINATION
Without limitation to such rights or remedies as CITY shall otherwise have by law, CITY shall have 
the right to terminate this Agreement or suspend work on the Project for any reason, upon ten (10) days' 
written notice to CONSULTANT.  CONSULTANT agrees to cease all work under this Agreement upon 
receipt of said written notice.
Upon termination and upon CITY's payment of the amount required to be paid, documents 
become the property of CITY, and CONSULTANT shall transfer them to CITY upon request without 
additional compensation.
SECTION 7 - OWNERSHIP OF DOCUMENTS
All documents prepared by CONSULTANT in the performance of this Agreement, although 
instruments of professional service, are and shall be the property of CITY, whether the project for 
which they are made is executed or not.

employees, and agents from and against any and all claims, loss, liability, damage, and expense arising 
out of CONSULTANT’s performance of this Agreement, except those claims arising out of CITY’s sole 
negligence or willful misconduct.  CONSULTANT agrees to defend City, its elected and appointed 
officials, employees, and agents against any such claims. The CONSULTANT’S duty to indemnify shall 
survive expiration or early termination of this Agreement.

thereafter (five years for building or major improvements) the insurance specified in Exhibit C to this 
Agreement.
SECTION 13 - NON-ASSIGNABILITY
Both parties hereto recognize that this Agreement is for the personal services of CONSULTANT 
and cannot be transferred, assigned, or subcontracted by CONSULTANT without the prior written 
consent of CITY.

unenforceable by a court of competent jurisdiction, the remaining provisions of this Agreement shall 
continue in full force and effect.
SECTION 17 - COSTS AND ATTORNEY FEES
Attorney fees in total amount not exceeding $5000, shall be recoverable as costs (by the filing 
of a cost bill) by the prevailing party in any action or actions to enforce the provisions of this 
Agreement.  The above $5000 limit is the total of attorney fees recoverable whether in the trial court, 
appellate court, or otherwise, and regardless of the number of attorneys, trials, appeals, or actions.  It 
is the intent of this Agreement that neither party shall have to pay the other more than $5000 for 
attorney fees arising out of an action, or actions to enforce the provisions of this Agreement.
SECTION 18 - NON-DISCRIMINATION

origin, ancestry, physical handicap, medical condition, marital status, sex, or age, unless based upon a 
bona fide occupational qualification pursuant to the California Fair Employment and Housing Act.

SECTION 19 - MEDIATION
Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be submitted to 
mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be 
agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one 
name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and 
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.
SECTION 20 - LITIGATION
CONSULTANT shall testify at CITY'S request if litigation is brought against CITY in connection 
with CONSULTANT's services under this Agreement.  Unless the action is brought by CONSULTANT, or 
is based upon CONSULTANT's wrongdoing, CITY shall compensate CONSULTANT for preparation for 
testimony, testimony, and travel at CONSULTANT's standard hourly rates at the time of actual 
testimony.

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
Service Tasks include but are not limited to:
1.
Survey Services
a.
Survey existing intersection from garage line or back-of-walk to centerline of street.
b.
Survey all hardscape, trees, utility boxes, and drain inlet rim elevations (include next closest 
inlet from the intersection on each leg of the intersection)
c.
Survey existing elevations of top of curb (TC), flowline (FL), lip of gutter, driveway approach, 
walkway, 5 foot AC conform, centerline, AC conform (25 feet from the center, all directions), 
30 ft past all returns
d.
Survey existing curb ramp: BC, POC, EC
e.
Survey private property such as driveways, patios, stairways, walkways, etc.
f.
Inverts of all storm systems within the limits of work
2.
Potholing and Underground Facility Locating Services
a.
Pre-inspection Activities (e.g. permitting and contacting 811 for Underground Service Alert 
markings
b.
Performing inspections and field tests in accordance with the latest edition of codes, 
standard, and specifications
c.
Locating utilities marked in field, including nondestructive methods
d.
Marking up of submitted drawings showing the determined location of underground 
facilities with a legend explaining the system and equipment used
e.
Compiling spreadsheet of information with pothole number, description of pothole location, 
pothole diameter, pothole depth, and findings

RECITALS:
A.  CITY desires certain on call construction management and inspection services 
hereinafter described.
B.  CITY desires to engage CONSULTANT to provide these on call construction 
management and inspection services by reason of its qualifications and experience for performing such 
services and CONSULTANT has offered to provide the required services on the terms and in the manner 
set forth herein.
NOW, THEREFORE, IT IS AGREED as follows:
SECTION 1 - SCOPE OF SERVICES
The scope of services to be performed by CONSULTANT under this Agreement is as described in 
Exhibit A to this Agreement, attached and incorporated by reference.
SECTION 2 - DUTIES OF CONSULTANT
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for the professional quality, technical accuracy and 
coordination of all work furnished by CONSULTANT under this Agreement.  CONSULTANT shall, without 
additional compensation, correct or revise any errors or deficiencies in its work.
CONSULTANT represents that it is qualified to furnish the services described under this 
Agreement.
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for employing or engaging all persons necessary to perform 
the services of CONSULTANT.
CONSULTANT agrees to comply with the City’s minimum wage ordinance as codified in 
Municipal Code Chapter 5.92, which differs from the state minimum wage and includes a Consumer 
Price Index escalator.
CONSULTANT and his subcontractors shall comply with State’s Prevailing Wage Laws.

agreement and be completed on December 31, 2025. This term of this Agreement may be extended by

CONSULTANT.

Payment shall be made by CITY only for services rendered and upon submission of a payment 
request upon completion and CITY approval of the work performed.  In consideration for the full

verified time and materials, in an amount of $300,000, pursuant to rates stated in Exhibit B to this 
Agreement, attached and incorporated by reference.
Cost adjustment for the second and subsequent year’s annual fixed amounts will be made using 
annual indexes of the “Consumer Price Index for All Urban Consumers,” Bay Area City Average, all 
items (1967=100) as published in the Monthly Review by the U.S. Department of Labor, (CPI). The 
annual increase in rates is not to exceed CPI or 3%, whichever is lower.
SECTION 6 - TERMINATION
Without limitation to such rights or remedies as CITY shall otherwise have by law, CITY shall have 
the right to terminate this Agreement or suspend work on the Project for any reason, upon ten (10) days' 
written notice to CONSULTANT.  CONSULTANT agrees to cease all work under this Agreement upon 
receipt of said written notice.
Upon termination and upon CITY's payment of the amount required to be paid, documents 
become the property of CITY, and CONSULTANT shall transfer them to CITY upon request without 
additional compensation.
SECTION 7 - OWNERSHIP OF DOCUMENTS

instruments of professional service, are and shall be the property of CITY, whether the project for 
which they are made is executed or not.

SECTION 18 - NON-DISCRIMINATION
CONSULTANT warrants that it is an Equal Opportunity Employer and shall comply with

SECTION 19 - MEDIATION
Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be submitted to 
mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be 
agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one 
name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and 
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.
SECTION 20 - LITIGATION
CONSULTANT shall testify at CITY'S request if litigation is brought against CITY in connection 
with CONSULTANT's services under this Agreement.  Unless the action is brought by CONSULTANT, or 
is based upon CONSULTANT's wrongdoing, CITY shall compensate CONSULTANT for preparation for 
testimony, testimony, and travel at CONSULTANT's standard hourly rates at the time of actual 
testimony.

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
Service Tasks include but are not limited to: 
1.
Project and Contract Administration
a.
Coordinate pre-construction and weekly progress meetings
b.
Evaluate schedule
c.
Communicate effectively and coordinate with the construction contractor and project 
manager
d.
Prepare and submit construction monthly progress reports
e.
Review contract documents, environmental documents, applicable laws and regulations
f.
Review Submittals, Requests for Information, Contractor monthly invoices, Contractor’s 
work, Change Orders
2.
Construction Observation, Inspection and Specialty Inspection
a.
Maintain daily inspection reports, including photos
b.
Review Construction Contractor’s compliance with permits as well as health & safety 
standards
c.
Coordinate any needed specialty inspections
3.
Change Order Management
a.
Coordinate, review, evaluate and recommend course of action for change order requests 
and submittals
4.
Constructability Reviews
5.
Construction Claims Analysis and Support
6.
Specialty Inspection Services
7.
Project Closeout and Acceptance Services
a.
Develop corrective item work lists and inspection of corrective actions performed
b.
Prepare and submit final construction report

EXHIBIT C
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate 
limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or 
the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONSULTANT has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and 
shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.

Rev 9/22
Notice of Cancellation
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City.
Waiver of Subrogation
CONSULTANT hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said 
CONSULTANT may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  
CONSULTANT agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of 
subrogation, but this provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of 
subrogation endorsement from the insurer.  
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the CONSULTANT to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof 
of ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within 
the retention.

CONSULTANT warrants that it is an Equal Opportunity Employer and shall comply with 
applicable regulations governing equal employment opportunity.  Neither CONSULTANT nor any of its 
subcontractors shall discriminate in the employment of any person because of race, color, national 
origin, ancestry, physical handicap, medical condition, marital status, sex, or age, unless based upon a 
bona fide occupational qualification pursuant to the California Fair Employment and Housing Act.
SECTION 19 - MEDIATION
Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be submitted to 
mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be 
agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one 
name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and 
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.
SECTION 20 - LITIGATION
CONSULTANT shall testify at CITY'S request if litigation is brought against CITY in connection 
with CONSULTANT's services under this Agreement.  Unless the action is brought by CONSULTANT, or 
is based upon CONSULTANT's wrongdoing, CITY shall compensate CONSULTANT for preparation for 
testimony, testimony, and travel at CONSULTANT's standard hourly rates at the time of actual 
testimony.

EXHIBIT C
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate 
limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or 
the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONSULTANT has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and 
shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.

Notice of Cancellation
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City.
Waiver of Subrogation
CONSULTANT hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said 
CONSULTANT may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  
CONSULTANT agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of 
subrogation, but this provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of 
subrogation endorsement from the insurer.  
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the CONSULTANT to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof 
of ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within 
the retention.  
Acceptability of Insurers
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless 
otherwise acceptable to the City.
Verification of Coverage
CONSULTANT shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies 
of the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause.  All certificates and 
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure 
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the CONSULTANT’s 
obligation to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

A.  CITY desires certain on call material testing services hereinafter described.

has offered to provide the required services on the terms and in the manner set forth herein.
NOW, THEREFORE, IT IS AGREED as follows:
SECTION 1 - SCOPE OF SERVICES
The scope of services to be performed by CONSULTANT under this Agreement is as described in 
Exhibit A to this Agreement, attached and incorporated by reference.
SECTION 2 - DUTIES OF CONSULTANT

coordination of all work furnished by CONSULTANT under this Agreement.  CONSULTANT shall, without 
additional compensation, correct or revise any errors or deficiencies in its work.
CONSULTANT represents that it is qualified to furnish the services described under this 
Agreement.
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for employing or engaging all persons necessary to perform 
the services of CONSULTANT.

Municipal Code Chapter 5.92, which differs from the state minimum wage and includes a Consumer 
Price Index escalator.
CONSULTANT and his subconsultants shall comply with State’s Prevailing Wage Laws.

Agreement, attached and incorporated by reference.
Cost adjustment for the second and subsequent year’s annual fixed amounts will be made using 
annual indexes of the “Consumer Price Index for All Urban Consumers,” Bay Area City Average, all 
items (1967=100) as published in the Monthly Review by the U.S. Department of Labor, (CPI). The 
annual increase in rates is not to exceed CPI or 3%, whichever is lower.
SECTION 6 - TERMINATION
Without limitation to such rights or remedies as CITY shall otherwise have by law, CITY shall have 
the right to terminate this Agreement or suspend work on the Project for any reason, upon ten (10) days' 
written notice to CONSULTANT.  CONSULTANT agrees to cease all work under this Agreement upon 
receipt of said written notice.
Upon termination and upon CITY's payment of the amount required to be paid, documents 
become the property of CITY, and CONSULTANT shall transfer them to CITY upon request without 
additional compensation.
SECTION 7 - OWNERSHIP OF DOCUMENTS

instruments of professional service, are and shall be the property of CITY, whether the project for 
which they are made is executed or not.

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
Service Tasks for material testing and reporting include but are not limited to sampling of material including 
asphalt concrete, portland cement concrete, slurry, emulsion, aggregate base, soils and other material as 
necessary for grading, paving, concrete work and other related testing.  The City will request services either 
by email or phone call and may give less than 48-hour notice.  All testing procedures must meet current 
Caltrans Material Testing Requirements.
Testing and reporting may include but are not limited to the following: 
1.
Soil Testing per Caltrans Standard Specifications
a.
Percent Compaction by Caltrans standards 
b.
Sand Equivalent 
c.
Moisture Content and Dry Density Determination
d.
Durability Index
e.
Unconfined Compressive Strength Test
f.
Atterberg Limits Test
g.
Gradation Analysis
h.
Resistance (R) Values
2.
Soil Sampling and Reporting
a.
Sampling and Chain of Custody Reporting
b.
Soil Analytical Composition and Classification Reporting
c.
Environmental Screening Levels Reporting
3.
Concrete Testing per Caltrans Standard Specifications
a.
Concrete Slump Testing
b.
Concrete Strength Testing 
4.
Asphalt Concrete Testing per Caltrans Standard Specifications

EXHIBIT C
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate 
limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or 
the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONSULTANT has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and 
shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.
183 of 265

--- page 184 ---
Professional Services
Page 13 of 13
Rev 9/22
Notice of Cancellation
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City.
Waiver of Subrogation
CONSULTANT hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said 
CONSULTANT may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  
CONSULTANT agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of 
subrogation, but this provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of 
subrogation endorsement from the insurer.  
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the CONSULTANT to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof 
of ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within 
the retention.  
Acceptability of Insurers
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless 
otherwise acceptable to the City.
Verification of Coverage
CONSULTANT shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies 
of the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause.  All certificates and 
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure 
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the CONSULTANT’s 
obligation to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

AGREEMENT WITH NICHOLS CONSULTING ENGINEERS, CHTD.
FOR PROFESSIONAL ON CALL CONSULTANT SERVICES
FOR 
 ENVIRONMENTAL & ENVIRONMENTAL COMPLIANCE SERVICES
This Agreement, made and entered into this day of ____________________, by and between 
the CITY OF SAN MATEO, a municipal corporation existing under the laws of the State of California 
(“CITY”), and Nichols Consulting Engineers, Chtd., a corporation, (“CONSULTANT” or “NCE”), with 
offices at 620 Coolidge Dr., Suite #100, Folsom, CA 95630.
RECITALS:
A.  CITY desires certain professional on call environmental and environmental 
compliance services hereinafter described.
B.  CITY desires to engage CONSULTANT to provide these professional on call 
environmental and environmental compliance services by reason of its qualifications and experience 
for performing such services and CONSULTANT has offered to provide the required services on the 
terms and in the manner set forth herein.
NOW, THEREFORE, IT IS AGREED as follows:
SECTION 1 - SCOPE OF SERVICES
The scope of services to be performed by CONSULTANT under this Agreement is as described in 
Exhibit A to this Agreement, attached and incorporated by reference.
SECTION 2 - DUTIES OF CONSULTANT
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for the professional quality, technical accuracy and 
coordination of all work furnished by CONSULTANT under this Agreement.  CONSULTANT shall, without 
additional compensation, correct or revise any errors or deficiencies in its work.
CONSULTANT represents that it is qualified to furnish the services described under this 
Agreement.
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for employing or engaging all persons necessary to perform 
the services of CONSULTANT.
CONSULTANT and his subconsultants shall comply with State’s Prevailing Wage Laws.
CONSULTANT agrees to comply with the City’s minimum wage ordinance as codified in 
Municipal Code Chapter 5.92, which differs from the state minimum wage and includes a Consumer 
Price Index escalator.
185 of 265

--- page 186 ---
Professional Services
Page 2 of 12
Rev 9/22
SECTION 3 - DUTIES OF CITY
CITY shall provide pertinent information regarding its requirements for the project.
CITY shall examine documents submitted by CONSULTANT and shall render decisions pertaining 
thereto promptly, to avoid unreasonable delay in the progress of CONSULTANT's work.
SECTION 4 - TERM
The services to be performed under this Agreement shall commence upon execution of this 
agreement and be completed on December 31, 2025. This term of this Agreement may be extended by 
written amendment executed by the Director of Public Works and a duly authorized representative of 
CONSULTANT.
SECTION 5 - PAYMENT
Payment shall be made by CITY only for services rendered and upon submission of a payment 
request upon completion and CITY approval of the work performed.  In consideration for the full 
performance of the services set forth in Exhibit A, CITY agrees to pay CONSULTANT a fee, based on 
verified time and materials, in an amount of $150,000, pursuant to rates stated in Exhibit B to this 
Agreement, attached and incorporated by reference.
Cost adjustment for the second and subsequent year’s annual fixed amounts will be made using 
annual indexes of the “Consumer Price Index for All Urban Consumers,” Bay Area City Average, all 
items (1967=100) as published in the Monthly Review by the U.S. Department of Labor, (CPI). The 
annual increase in rates is not to exceed CPI or 3%, whichever is lower.
SECTION 6 - TERMINATION
Without limitation to such rights or remedies as CITY shall otherwise have by law, CITY shall have 
the right to terminate this Agreement or suspend work on the Project for any reason, upon ten (10) days' 
written notice to CONSULTANT.  CONSULTANT agrees to cease all work under this Agreement upon 
receipt of said written notice.
Upon termination and upon CITY's payment of the amount required to be paid, documents 
become the property of CITY, and CONSULTANT shall transfer them to CITY upon request without 
additional compensation.
SECTION 7 - OWNERSHIP OF DOCUMENTS
All documents prepared by CONSULTANT in the performance of this Agreement, although 
instruments of professional service, are and shall be the property of CITY, whether the project for 
which they are made is executed or not.

SECTION 8 - CONFIDENTIALITY
All reports and documents prepared by CONSULTANT in connection with the performance of 
this Agreement are confidential until released by CITY to the public.  CONSULTANT shall not make any 
such documents or information available to any individual or organization not employed by 
CONSULTANT or CITY without the written consent of CITY before any such release.
SECTION 9 - INTEREST OF CONSULTANT
CONSULTANT covenants that it presently has no interest, and shall not acquire any interest, 
direct or indirect, financial or otherwise, which would conflict in any manner or degree with the 
performance of the services under this Agreement.
SECTION 10 - CONSULTANT'S STATUS
It is expressly agreed that in the performance of the professional services required under this 
Agreement, CONSULTANT shall at all times be considered an independent contractor as defined in 
Labor Code Section 3353, under control of the CITY as to the result of the work but not the means by 
which the result is accomplished.  Nothing herein shall be construed to make CONSULTANT an agent or 
employee of CITY while providing services under this Agreement.
SECTION 11 - INDEMNITY
CONSULTANT agrees to hold harmless and indemnify CITY, its elected and appointed officials, 
employees, and agents from and against any and all claims, loss, liability, damage, and expense arising 
out of CONSULTANT’s performance of this Agreement, except those claims arising out of CITY’s sole 
negligence or willful misconduct.  CONSULTANT agrees to defend City, its elected and appointed 
officials, employees, and agents against any such claims. The CONSULTANT’S duty to indemnify shall 
survive expiration or early termination of this Agreement.
SECTION 12 - INSURANCE
CONSULTANT shall procure and maintain for the duration of the contract and three years 
thereafter (five years for building or major improvements) the insurance specified in Exhibit C to this 
Agreement.
SECTION 13 - NON-ASSIGNABILITY
Both parties hereto recognize that this Agreement is for the personal services of CONSULTANT 
and cannot be transferred, assigned, or subcontracted by CONSULTANT without the prior written 
consent of CITY.

SECTION 14 - RELIANCE UPON PROFESSIONAL
SKILL OF CONSULTANT
It is mutually understood and agreed by and between the parties hereto that CONSULTANT is 
skilled in the professional calling necessary to perform the work agreed to be done under this 
Agreement and that CITY relies upon the skill of CONSULTANT to do and perform the work in the most 
skillful manner, and CONSULTANT agrees to thus perform the work.  The acceptance of CONSULTANT's 
work by CITY does not operate as a release of CONSULTANT from said obligation.
SECTION 15 - WAIVERS
The waiver by either party of any breach or violation of any term, covenant, or condition of this 
Agreement or of any provisions of any ordinance or law shall not be deemed to be a waiver of such 
term, covenant, condition, ordinance or law or of any subsequent breach or violation of the same or of 
any other term, condition, ordinance, or law.  The subsequent acceptance by either party of any fee or 
other money which may become due hereunder shall not be deemed to be a waiver of any preceding 
breach or violation by the other party of any term, covenant, or condition of this Agreement or of any 
applicable law or ordinance.
SECTION 16 - SEVERABILITY
If any term or portion of this Agreement is held to be invalid, illegal, or otherwise 
unenforceable by a court of competent jurisdiction, the remaining provisions of this Agreement shall 
continue in full force and effect.
SECTION 17 - COSTS AND ATTORNEY FEES
Attorney fees in total amount not exceeding $5000, shall be recoverable as costs (by the filing 
of a cost bill) by the prevailing party in any action or actions to enforce the provisions of this 
Agreement.  The above $5000 limit is the total of attorney fees recoverable whether in the trial court, 
appellate court, or otherwise, and regardless of the number of attorneys, trials, appeals, or actions.  It 
is the intent of this Agreement that neither party shall have to pay the other more than $5000 for 
attorney fees arising out of an action, or actions to enforce the provisions of this Agreement.
SECTION 18 - NON-DISCRIMINATION
CONSULTANT warrants that it is an Equal Opportunity Employer and shall comply with 
applicable regulations governing equal employment opportunity.  Neither CONSULTANT nor any of its 
subcontractors shall discriminate in the employment of any person because of race, color, national 
origin, ancestry, physical handicap, medical condition, marital status, sex, or age, unless based upon a 
bona fide occupational qualification pursuant to the California Fair Employment and Housing Act.

SECTION 19 - MEDIATION
Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be submitted to 
mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be 
agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one 
name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and 
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.
SECTION 20 - LITIGATION
CONSULTANT shall testify at CITY'S request if litigation is brought against CITY in connection 
with CONSULTANT's services under this Agreement.  Unless the action is brought by CONSULTANT, or 
is based upon CONSULTANT's wrongdoing, CITY shall compensate CONSULTANT for preparation for 
testimony, testimony, and travel at CONSULTANT's standard hourly rates at the time of actual 
testimony.
SECTION 21 - NOTICES
All notices hereunder shall be given in writing and mailed, postage prepaid, addressed as 
follows:

or oral.

SECTION 24 - GOVERNING LAW AND VENUE
This Agreement shall be governed by the laws of the State of California and, in the event of 
litigation, venue will be in the County of San Mateo.

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
Service Tasks include but are not limited to:
1.
Environmental regulatory compliance support 
2.
Health and safety regulation compliance support
3.
Technical support to manage environmental releases related to illicit discharge and hazardous spill 
response, including investigation, clean-up, and disposal oversight, and supporting the City with 
external regulatory agency notifications and communications
4.
Environmental sampling and characterization, including collecting and analyzing air, soil, 
groundwater, and surface water samples.
a.
Review of sampling, including those done by others
5.
Conduct environmental assessments including:
a.
Natural resource surveys (biological, cultural, etc.)
b.
Groundwater investigations
c.
Human health/ecological risk assessments
6.
NEPA/CEQA documentation and support 
a.
Waste characterization and regulatory support including sampling, hazardous waste 
determination, and disposal and re-use options
b.
Comprehensive Air Quality Compliance Services, including California Accidental Release 
Prevention (CalARP)
c.
Consulting for cost-effective solutions for the transport and disposal of contaminated 
material to appropriate disposal facilities
d.
Prepare and/or update Spill Prevention, Control, and Countermeasures (SPCC) plans
e.
Preparing and obtaining jurisdictional permits for City projects
f.
Conducting environmental audits for City facilities and projects
g.
Environmental regulatory compliance training and support with the development of 
standards and protocols to support and improve City routine operations.

CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).

insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.

SUBJECT:
 2750 South Delaware Street Access Easement – Acceptance  
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to accept the Grant of Access Easement on 2750 South Delaware Street; and authorize the City 
Manager to execute the Grant of Access Easement in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
A 36-inch City storm drainpipe conveys stormwater runoff from South El Camino Real into an existing drainage channel 
within Peninsula Corridor Joint Powers Board (PCJPB) Right-of-Way, adjacent to the western border of 2750 South 
Delaware Street. The drainage channel flows north into a 48-inch City storm drainpipe that leads to Borel Creek. 
Historically, Public Works has maintained the drainage channel within the PCJPB Right-of-Way on an annual and as-needed 
basis to prevent flooding issues. Public Works traverses the private property at 2750 South Delaware Street to access the 
channel through an existing 20-foot wide Public Service Easement (PSE) along the property’s western border. Due to the 
Bay Meadows Station Block 1 development at 2750 S. Delaware Street, channel access is now limited to the northern tip of 
the property and project driveway. The northern tip of the property is not covered by the 20-foot-wide PSE. Public Works 
cannot access the channel through the new Hillsdale Caltrain Station parking lot in PCJPB Right-of-Way due to the parking 
lot’s distance from the channel and trees obstructing access to the channel. 
The property owner of 2750 South Delaware Street, Bay Meadows Station 1 Investors, LLC, agrees to grant an access 
easement to the City of San Mateo on, across, and over the northern tip of their property not covered by the PSE for 
maintenance of the drainage channel. The Grant of Easement includes language that allows the Grantor to relocate the 
easement if an alternate point of access is identified and agreed upon by the Grantor and City of San Mateo. 
The access easement was originally approved by Council on July 18, 2022. However, the County of San Mateo rejected 
recordation of the access easement document, as the document did not include a legal description. The applicant's 
Licensed Surveyor prepared a plat and legal description for the access easement. The City's contracted Licensed Surveyor 
determined the plat and legal description to be technically correct. 
The easement allows operations and maintenance staff the proper rights to maintain the channel and prevent flooding 
issues. Staff recommends accepting the proposed access easement with plat and legal description.  
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budgetary impact for accepting the access easement.

In accordance with CEQA Guidelines section 15061(b)(3), accepting the access easement is exempt from CEQA as 
acceptance of an easement will not have a significant effect on the environment.

Easement (PSE) along the property’s Western border to access the channel; and

Easement, set forth in Exhibit A attached hereto.

with the San Mateo County Recorder’s Office.

Community Development Department
MEETING DATE:
September 05, 2023 
SUBJECT:
Grand Jury Report: “Accessory Dwelling Units: Affordable Housing’s Panacea or Prevarication?” – Response Letter  
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve a letter responding to the June 12, 2023, San Mateo County Civil Grand Jury report entitled, "Accessory Dwelling 
Units: Affordable Housing's Panacea or Prevarication?" and authorize the Mayor to send the response letter on behalf of 
the City Council. 
BACKGROUND:
Since 1969, California has required that all local governments (cities and counties) adequately plan to meet the housing 
needs of their community. California’s local governments meet this requirement by adopting housing elements, which are 
updated every 8 years. Housing elements are one of several "chapters," or elements, of a city’s General Plan, and are 
required by the State. Housing elements are the only element of a General Plan subject to State requirements for content, 
and they must be certified by the California Department of Housing and Community Development (HCD). 
 
For the upcoming eight-year housing element cycle (2023-2031), HCD has identified the nine-county Bay Area region’s 
housing need to be 441,176 units, with this number broken down into four income categories, from very low-income 
households (which includes extremely low) to above moderate (market rate) housing. This Regional Housing Needs 
Determination (RHND) is based on population projections produced by the California Department of Finance (DOF), as well 
as adjustments that incorporate the region’s existing housing need. 
 
The City of San Mateo’s Regional Housing Needs Assessment (RHNA) for this housing cycle is 7,015 new housing units 
distributed across the four income groups: very low, low, moderate, and above moderate. The City’s Adopted Housing 
Element identifies how the City can accommodate its RHNA of 7,015 new homes over the next eight years, plus a buffer, 
and establishes goals, policies, and programs to help address the City’s current and future housing needs. These goals, 
policies, and programs are required to be accompanied by a list of eligible land resources and a Sites Inventory identified 
for planned residential development to accommodate the RHNA. HCD guidance stipulates that a projection of Accessory 
Dwelling Units (ADUs) expected to be built within the eight-year planning period can also be counted as part of the 
inventory. Based on permitting data, the City anticipates that 440 of the 7,015 units of the RHNA allocation (6%) would be 
ADUs.
 
San Mateo County Civil Grand Jury Report
On June 12, 2023, the San Mateo County Civil Grand Jury released a report entitled “Accessory Dwelling Units: Affordable 
Housing‘s Panacea or Prevarication?” (Attachment 2). The issue explored in this report is the possible misuse and over-
reliance by some County of San Mateo communities on ADUs to meet their Regional Housing Needs Allocation (RHNA) 
requirements for very low, low, and moderate income units in the current housing cycle (2023-2031) in order to avoid 
developing multifamily affordable housing. The report notes that the State has made significant changes in the ADU laws 
206 of 265

--- page 207 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
to address the current housing needs, which include numerous Senate and Assembly bills which were enacted in 2018 and 
2020. These laws required local jurisdictions to significantly reduce development requirements for ADUs and streamline 
the permitting process to increase production since ADUs have been identified as a housing type that can provide 
additional units at all income categories.
 
The report noted that San Mateo County jurisdictions have almost unanimously adopted the Association of Bay Area 
Governments (ABAG) percentage formula based on surveys to determine income affordability rather than actual usage of 
constructed ADUs. The formula allocates affordability levels to ADUs as follows: 30% Very Low Income, 30% Low Income, 
30% Moderate and 10% Above Moderate. The report also noted that if HCD approves the County of San Mateo’s 
jurisdictions currently drafted Housing Elements, the County may end up with many affordable units that exist only on 
paper because they are counted as affordable by HCD but will not be made available or occupied by those who are actually 
income eligible.
 
Based on permitting history from the past four years (2019-2022), the City has issued an average of 60 building permits for 
new ADUs. The City’s Housing Element includes a conservatively lower estimate of 55 ADUs annually, for a total of 440 
ADUs over the next eight years, for this housing cycle. Based on HCD-approved ABAG ADU survey, the City updated its 
breakdown to the 30-30-30-10 formula to estimate ADU affordability.  This results in approximately 132 very low-income 
units, 132 low-income units, 132 moderate-income units and 44 above moderate- income units. However, it should be 
noted that the ADU production estimate represents only 6% of the City’s total RHNA of 7,015 units, and only 4.5% of the 
total sites inventory capacity of 9,944 units. In addition to ADUs, the City’s sites inventory includes several additional 
categories of sites, including pipeline projects, previous RHNA Cycle 5 sites, sites anticipated to redevelop, and vacant sites 
zoned for residential use.
 
The Report contains seven findings and six recommendations. Every jurisdiction in the County, including the City of San 
Mateo, has been asked to submit a response letter to the Honorable Judge Nancy L. Fineman no later than September 11, 
2023. The City’s response must be approved by the Council at a public meeting. Staff has prepared a draft response letter 
for the Council’s review and approval. (Attachment 2). 
 
The City provided responses to each of the findings and recommendations. The City’s responses to the seven findings and 
six recommendations are summarized in Table 1 below. More detailed responses are provided in the draft response letter.
 
  Table 1: San Mateo Grand Jury Report on ADUs - Responses to Findings/Recommendations 
 Finding
 City Response
F1. Due to recent changes in California ADU-related laws, local 
governments cannot condition ADU permits in San Mateo County 
on complying with affordability monitoring and verification.   
 City agrees.
F2. San Mateo County and most of its municipalities rely on ADUs 
to meet their affordable housing commitments in their RHNA-6 
plans.
 City partially agrees.
F3. Atherton, Hillsborough, Portola Valley, and Woodside rely on 
ADUs to meet as much as 80 percent of their affordable housing 
commitments in their RHNA-6 plans.
 Not applicable.
F4. HCD has instructed San Mateo County jurisdictions to monitor 
and verify future ADU production and affordability every two 
years but has yet to specify how to verify whether very low-, low- 
or moderate-income households are occupying the ADUs as 
planned.   
 City partially agrees.
 F5. Other than Brisbane and Redwood City, San Mateo County 
and its jurisdictions have yet to articulate how they will monitor 
and verify ADU production or affordability.   
 City does not agree.
 F6. Without effective ADU monitoring and verification, it will be 
impossible to evaluate whether the jurisdictions are meeting their 
RHNA-6 obligations for low-, very-low, and moderate-income 
 City does not agree.
207 of 265

--- page 208 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
housing units.
F7. ADU affordability and occupancy could be monitored by 
agencies such as HIP Housing which has proven systems and 
processes to verify occupancy of deed-restricted rental properties 
in San Mateo County.   
 City agrees.
 Recommendation
 City Response
R1. San Mateo County and each City should immediately stop 
using ADUs to meet their State-mandated very low-, low-, and 
moderate-income housing targets in their Housing Element 
submissions until they have also proposed an effective 
monitoring system that verifies how newly developed ADU’s will 
be used. 
Recommendation will not be implemented.
R2. By February 1, 2024, San Mateo County and each City should 
develop, adopt, and implement a verification system capable of 
monitoring and verifying how newly developed ADU’s are being 
used.
Part of the recommendation has yet to be 
implemented but will be implemented in 
the future, and part of the 
recommendation is not warranted.
  
R3. By February 1, 2024, San Mateo County and each City should 
develop and adopt incentives for ADU owners which could be 
offered in exchange for deed restrictions that would include 
requirements for ADU tenants to participate in independent 
monitoring.   
The City agrees with the goal of adopting 
an affordable ADU program.
R4. By February 1, 2024, San Mateo County and each City should 
track the intended use of ADUs – rented or non-rented – during 
the permitting process and offer incentives in exchange for deed 
restrictions that require ADUs to be used as rentals.   
This recommendation has yet to be 
implemented but will be implemented in 
the future.
  
R5. By April 1, 2024, San Mateo County and each City should 
develop and adopt a new ADU affordability distribution formula 
specific to each jurisdiction to the extent they are used for 
meeting the very low-, low-, and moderate-income housing 
requirements in their RHNA housing elements.
The recommendation will not be 
implemented.
R6. San Mateo County and each City should consider working 
together to address Recommendations 2 and 3.  
The recommendation has been 
implemented.

There is no budget impact for this administrative action.
